<Review>I heard about Sweet Blessings on a Be Localish segment on the news.  It's not easy finding good southern style comfort food in L.A.  When I finally stopped by this weekend. I was greeted very nicely. Upon reviewing the menu, I couldn't make up my mind. Everything sounded so good. I asked for a recommendation as it was my first time. A very nice man who worked there advised I could get a salmon/crab cake a la carte and definitely try the gumbo.  So that's what I ordered. And I absolutely had to try the peach/ mango cobbler.
Let me just say that everyone at the restaurant was so nice. I did not wait too long for my order. When I got home and took my food out, it smelled great!
It also tasted Great!  The gumbo was so well seasoned.  It did not have any unnecessary bell peppers which I was so happy about. It was probably the best gumbo I've had in the city.  The salmon/ crab cake was delicious and cooked perfectly.  It had very nice grilled flavor and was a good size portion. It did not come with a sauce, but after the first bite, You don't need a sauce. It stands on it's own.  The cobbler was so yummy. Not too bready or too sweet. Everything tasted incredibly fresh. Made with care. As it should be.  The Blessing is, I finally made it over there.  I will Absolutely go back. I cannot wait to try more items on the menu. I'm so happy I stopped in and I'm so glad that nice man helped me choose what to order. Happy happy Belly!  Probably the best new food to go order experience I have had in months. < review>
I heard about Sweet Blessings on a Be Localish segment on the news.  It's not easy finding good southern style comfort food in L.A.  When I finally stopped by this weekend. I was greeted very nicely. Upon reviewing the menu, I couldn't make up my mind. Everything sounded so good. I asked for a recommendation as it was my first time. A very nice man who worked there advised I could get a salmon/crab cake a la carte and definitely try the gumbo.  So that's what I ordered. And I absolutely had to try the peach/ mango cobbler.
Let me just say that everyone at the restaurant was so nice. I did not wait too long for my order. When I got home and took my food out, it smelled great!
It also tasted Great!  The gumbo was so well seasoned.  It did not have any unnecessary bell peppers which I was so happy about. It was probably the best gumbo I've had in the city.  The salmon/ crab cake was delicious and cooked perfectly.  It had very nice grilled flavor and was a good size portion. It did not come with a sauce, but after the first bite, You don't need a sauce. It stands on it's own.  The cobbler was so yummy. Not too bready or too sweet. Everything tasted incredibly fresh. Made with care. As it should be.  The Blessing is, I finally made it over there.  I will Absolutely go back. I cannot wait to try more items on the menu. I'm so happy I stopped in and I'm so glad that nice man helped me choose what to order. Happy happy Belly!  Probably the best new food to go order experience I have had in months.   Thank you Sweet Blessings ‚ù§< /review>

< Review>
My dog Brody has been swimming before, but was always afraid of the water. He had his first swim lesson here at Doggie Central today. The instructor was so patient and friendly! By the end he was jumping into the pool himself. They had plenty of toys to grab his attention, and they provide towels to dry your dog after the lesson. She even cleaned his ears for me. Swimming lessons are only offered on weekends and the spots fill up quickly so call ahead to book early. I've also walked in for a bath before and they were able to take him right away. Highly recommend this place for your pet!</Review>

I found Doggie Central on the internet and thought I would give them a try with aquatic therapy.  Within 2 weeks of working with Tony, the canine aquatic trainer, Brownie (my Golden Retriever mix) had no more limp and was able to get up without any difficulty. I wish that I had started Brownie years ago with aquatic training because I've seen the physical benefit of it. We commute from Simi Valley to train with Tony.  I would totally recommend aquatic training at DC with Tony for anyone who wants to increase his/her dog's quality of health.< /Text>

Great bang for your buck, as far as storage options go near the Bay Area. The buildings were always clean inside and out every time I went there. They offer free dollies to use, but most of the time I've been there they were all in use - be prepared to bring your own dollies if you are moving a lot here.

I had my items stored here for over a year - no problems at all. If you live in SF and need long-term storage, but don't want to spend over $150/month on a 10x15 space, head here for a deal.</text>

<review>Best McLane I've been to. My appointment was at 1130 and I arrived the day before and was parked on mid-counties road so I could check-in at 1000.
Quiet street and wasn't bothered by anyone, there's a black bear not far that you can walk to our bobtail to.
The morning of my appointment, I got a knock on the truck at 0800 with someone from McClane saying they could get me in a door ASAP. Have him the bills and he told me any door from 28-32. Docked into 30 and then walked over and checked in at for 19. Waited in the truck for someone to check and cut the seal. Opened doors and backed in at 0830. Iliana's food truck stops in for drivers to get real food or snacks. I was unloaded by 1000 and able to park back on the street until I got my next load. Again, great mclane!</review>< Pics>

<user_name>Sabrina Shore<//user_name><date>1611360788175< /date><Rate>5< /Rate>< Review>
Excellent AF! Food truck located in a little strip mall that serves birria dishes. I ordered several things. The birria itself is tender, juicy and flavorful...like the carnitas of beef. BirriaRamen was awesome! Now, it's not like authentic ramen so go to a ramen place for that but the consome, the beef and the noodle combo is delightful. The birria quesadilla lacked serious presentation. I didn't think I was going to like it. It was greasy and sort of limp but it was super good tasting despite all that. Lol. It was also gigantic! I also got the taco and quesotaco and a side of consome. Both tacos were good but I did like the queso taco slightly more. Pour that consome on top and u r golden. Didn't even use the salsa which I normally require on my Mexican food. Reasonably priced. This place is good!! Birria, yum!<//Review>

<Review>TL;DR - Ripped off, poor service, lied to, awful food :(

My boyfriend and I visited the restaurant after looking up the menus online, and we checked the menus outside the restaurant on Thanksgiving Day (it was closed for the holiday). The menus posted outside and online were the same. When we visited the restaurant the next day the menus seemed to be different, so I asked the waitress if they had changed their menus. She told us that nothing had changed, but asked me to show the menu I had seen online. When I showed it to her, she immediately broke into a loud outburst (which every nearby table could overhear) telling me that there was no way the restaurant could continue serving fish at such a price. That doesn't bother me - we're happy to order off the updated menus, but she didn't need to make such a scene.

We ordered 1 order (2 pieces each) of toro, maguro, halibut, and uni. The halibut and uni were listed as market price, while the toro and maguro were around $6.50 - $7.00 each. Then, we ordered 6 pcs. of oysters (around $14.00) and one order of ebi tempura ($8.50).
- Ebi tempura: only 3 pieces for $8.50? Nothing was of epic high quality, so we didn't appreciate the portion size. This seemed too high for some simple tempura.
- 6 pc. oysters: they served it to us at the end of the meal when the ice bed under the oysters had already melted. This means that they had waited for quite a while before serving us the oysters. The (tiny) oysters were drowning in an overpowering, acidic sauce. I didn't even want to finish the order.
- The sushi was bad, too. The quality of the fish did NOT seem exceptional or even average. It was under-average. The uni was especially bad. We felt sick all day after eating it. The waitress had advertised the uni and halibut as being especially fresh and highly recommended we order it.

Aside from the sub-par food, the worst part of our experience was what happened when we got our bill. It was around $85 (up to $90+ with tip) for 8 pieces of sushi, 3 pieces of shrimp tempura, and 6 tiny oysters. This is ridiculous. When we asked for our itemized receipt, we noticed that the halibut and uni had been listed as $20 EACH. This is $20 for 2 PIECES of sushi while the other sushi prices were nowhere close. We have previously dined at highly rated sushi restaurants in other parts of Canada and the US, and this price (for sushi) was even beyond what we paid at luxurious, high-end sushi restaurants. We don't mind spending the money for quality, we love sushi! We asked our waitress what happened with the bill, and she went on another rampage, talking about the shortage of fish in the USA and the high price of toro and how hard it was to catch fish. Umm.... if that's really the case, then why haven't the prices at the other restaurants risen so high? She kept arguing without listening to what we had to say - we never raised our voices or said anything rude, and politely tried to explain our confusion. She wouldn't listen and didn't budge.

I didn't really want to write such a negative review - I know that restaurants struggle, and that business is hard - but we would have appreciated more courtesy and transparency, as well as more honesty from the waitress.

Specific requests for the restaurant:
- Update your online menus.
- Be transparent about how much "market price" means. If a guest orders something that is listed as "market price", it is common courtesy to inform them of the price.
- Don't complain about how hard it is to catch fish when someone is confused about their bill.<//Review><Pics>None</Pics>< Response>
